id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="LGBT rights in the United Arab Emirates">Homosexuality</a> is illegal and is a <a href="/wiki/Capital_offence" class="mw-redirect" title="Capital offence">capital offence</a> in the UAE.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-arc.com_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arc.com-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> In 2013, an Emirati man was on trial for being accused of a "gay handshake".<sup id="cite_ref-arc.com_225-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arc.com-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> Article 80 of the Abu Dhabi Penal Code makes sodomy punishable with imprisonment of up to 14 years, while article 177 of the Penal Code of Dubai imposes imprisonment of up to 10 years on consensual sodomy.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Amputation" title="Amputation">Amputation</a> is a legal punishment in the UAE due to the Sharia courts.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Crucifixion" title="Crucifixion">Crucifixion</a> is a legal punishment in the UAE.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup> Article 1 of the Federal Penal Code states that "provisions of the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Law" class="mw-redirect" title="Islamic Law">Islamic Law</a> shall apply to the crimes of doctrinal punishment, punitive punishment and blood money."<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> The Federal Penal Code repealed only those provisions within the penal codes of individual emirates which are contradictory to the Federal Penal Code. Hence, both are enforceable simultaneously.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the month of <a href="/wiki/Ramadan" title="Ramadan">Ramadan</a>, it is illegal to publicly eat, drink, or smoke between sunrise and sunset.<sup id="cite_ref-ramadan_237-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ramadan-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> Exceptions are made for pregnant women and children. The law applies to both Muslims and non-Muslims,<sup id="cite_ref-ramadan_237-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ramadan-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> and failure to comply may result in arrest.<sup id="cite_ref-Riazat_Butt_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Riazat_Butt-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup> Dancing in public is illegal in the UAE.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Arab_Emirates&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="Human rights in the United Arab Emirates">Human rights in the United Arab Emirates</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Flogging" class="mw-redirect" title="Flogging">Flogging</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stoning" title="Stoning">stoning</a> are legal punishments in the UAE. The requirement is derived from <a href="/wiki/Sharia_law" class="mw-redirect" title="Sharia law">Sharia law</a>, and has been federal law since 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_242-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-242">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup> Some domestic workers in the UAE are victims of the country's interpretations of Sharia judicial punishments such as flogging and stoning.<sup id="cite_ref-drm_174-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-drm-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> The annual <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a> report on <a href="/wiki/Freedom_in_the_World" title="Freedom in the World">Freedom in the World</a> has listed the United Arab Emirates as "Not Free" every year since 1999, the first year for which records are available on their website.<sup id="cite_ref-United_Arab_Emirates_Reports_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-United_Arab_Emirates_Reports-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stop_UK_Arms_Exports_to_Saudi_UAE_Dictatorships_!.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Stop_UK_Arms_Exports_to_Saudi_UAE_Dictatorships_%21.jpg/220px-Stop_UK_Arms_Exports_to_Saudi_UAE_Dictatorships_%21.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="219" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Stop_UK_Arms_Exports_to_Saudi_UAE_Dictatorships_%21.jpg/330px-Stop_UK_Arms_Exports_to_Saudi_UAE_Dictatorships_%21.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Stop_UK_Arms_Exports_to_Saudi_UAE_Dictatorships_%21.jpg/440px-Stop_UK_Arms_Exports_to_Saudi_UAE_Dictatorships_%21.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2474" data-file-height="2458" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stop_UK_Arms_Exports_to_Saudi_UAE_Dictatorships_!.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Protest against the <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabian-led_intervention_in_Yemen" title="Saudi Arabian-led intervention in Yemen">Saudi Arabian-led intervention in Yemen</a>, March 2018</div></div></div>
<p>The UAE has escaped the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Spring" title="Arab Spring">Arab Spring</a>; however, more than 100 Emirati activists were jailed and <a href="/wiki/Tortured" class="mw-redirect" title="Tortured">tortured</a> because they sought reforms.<sup id="cite_ref-amnesty.org_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amnesty.org-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-amnesty_244-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amnesty-244">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup> Since 2011, the UAE government has increasingly carried out <a href="/wiki/Forced_disappearances" class="mw-redirect" title="Forced disappearances">forced disappearances</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-aohr_246-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aohr-246">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-hrw_247-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrw-247">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup> Many foreign nationals and Emirati citizens have been arrested and abducted by the state. The UAE government denies these people are being held (to conceal their whereabouts), placing these people outside the protection of the law.<sup id="cite_ref-amnesty_244-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amnesty-244">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-aohr_246-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aohr-246">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-forced_251-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forced-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup> According to Human Rights Watch, the reports of forced disappearance and torture in the UAE are of grave concern.<sup id="cite_ref-hrw_247-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrw-247">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Arab_Organization_for_Human_Rights" title="Arab Organization for Human Rights">Arab Organization for Human Rights</a> has obtained testimonies from many defendants, for its report on "Forced Disappearance and Torture in the UAE", who reported that they had been kidnapped, tortured and abused in detention centres.<sup id="cite_ref-aohr_246-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aohr-246">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-forced_251-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forced-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup> The report included 16 different methods of torture including severe beatings, threats with <a href="/wiki/Electrocution" title="Electrocution">electrocution</a> and denying access to medical care.<sup id="cite_ref-aohr_246-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aohr-246">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-forced_251-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forced-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2013, 94 Emirati activists were held in secret detention centres and put on trial for allegedly attempting to overthrow the government.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup> Human rights organizations have spoken out against the secrecy of the trial. An Emirati, whose father is among the defendants, was arrested for tweeting about the trial. In April 2013, he was sentenced to 10 months in jail.<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup> The latest forced disappearance involves <a href="/wiki/Disappearance_of_the_Al-Suwaidi_sisters" title="Disappearance of the Al-Suwaidi sisters">three sisters from Abu Dhabi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Amnesty_254-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Amnesty-254">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RTFeb15_255-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RTFeb15-255">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Repressive measures were also used against non-Emiratis in order to justify the UAE government's claim that there is an "international plot" in which UAE citizens and foreigners were working together to destabilize the country.<sup id="cite_ref-forced_251-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forced-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup> Foreign nationals were also subjected to a campaign of deportations.<sup id="cite_ref-forced_251-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forced-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup> There are many documented cases of Egyptians and other foreign nationals who had spent years working in the UAE and were then given only a few days to leave the country.<sup id="cite_ref-forced_251-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forced-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Foreign nationals subjected to forced disappearance include two <a href="/wiki/Libyans" class="mw-redirect" title="Libyans">Libyans</a><sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup> and two Qataris.<sup id="cite_ref-forced_251-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forced-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-qta_257-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qta-257">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup> Amnesty reported that the Qatari men have been abducted by the UAE government and the UAE government has withheld information about the men's fate from their families.<sup id="cite_ref-forced_251-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forced-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-qta_257-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qta-257">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup> Amongst the foreign nationals detained, imprisoned and expelled is <a href="/wiki/Iyad_El-Baghdadi" class="mw-redirect" title="Iyad El-Baghdadi">Iyad El-Baghdadi</a>, a popular blogger and Twitter personality.<sup id="cite_ref-forced_251-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forced-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup> He was arrested by UAE authorities, detained, imprisoned and then expelled from the country.<sup id="cite_ref-forced_251-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forced-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup> Despite his lifetime residence in the UAE, as a Palestinian citizen, El-Baghdadi had no recourse to contest this order.<sup id="cite_ref-forced_251-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forced-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup> He could not be deported back to the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_territories" title="Palestinian territories">Palestinian territories</a>, therefore he was deported to Malaysia.<sup id="cite_ref-forced_251-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forced-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2007, the UAE government attempted to cover up information on the rape of a French teenage boy by three Emirati locals, one of whose HIV-positive status was hidden by Emirati authorities.<sup id="cite_ref-nov1rapecase_258-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nov1rapecase-258">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup> Diplomatic pressure led to the arrest and conviction of the Emirati rapists.<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2009, a video tape of <a href="/wiki/Torture" title="Torture">torture</a> smuggled out of the UAE showed Sheikh <a href="/wiki/Issa_bin_Zayed_Al_Nahyan" title="Issa bin Zayed Al Nahyan">Issa bin Zayed Al Nahyan</a> torturing a man (Mohammed Shah Poor) with whips, electric cattle prods, wooden planks with protruding nails and running him over repeatedly with a car.<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup> In December 2009, Issa appeared in court and proclaimed his innocence.<sup id="cite_ref-Bakr1_261-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bakr1-261">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup> The trial ended on 10 January 2010, when Issa was cleared of the torture of Mohammed Shah Poor.<sup id="cite_ref-Bakr2_262-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bakr2-262">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> criticised the trial and called on the government to establish an independent body to investigate allegations of abuse by UAE security personnel and other persons of authority.<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/US_State_Department" class="mw-redirect" title="US State Department">US State Department</a> has expressed concern over the verdict and said all members of Emirati society "must stand equal before the law" and called for a careful review of the decision to ensure that the demands of justice are fully met in this case.<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In recent years, a large number of <a href="/wiki/Shia_Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Shia Muslim">Shia Muslim</a> expatriates have been deported from the UAE.<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup> Lebanese Shia families in particular have been deported for their alleged sympathy for <a href="/wiki/Hezbollah" title="Hezbollah">Hezbollah</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup> According to some organizations, more than 4,000 Shia expatriates have been deported from the UAE in recent years.<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The issue of <a href="/wiki/Sexual_abuse" title="Sexual abuse">sexual abuse</a> among female <a href="/wiki/Domestic_workers" class="mw-redirect" title="Domestic workers">domestic workers</a> is another area of concern, particularly given that domestic servants are not covered by the UAE labour law of 1980 or the draft labour law of 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup> Worker protests have been suppressed and protesters imprisoned without due process.<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup> In its 2013 Annual Report, <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a> drew attention to the United Arab Emirates' poor record on a number of human rights issues. They highlighted the government's restrictive approach to freedom of speech and assembly, their use of arbitrary arrest and torture, and UAE's use of the death penalty.<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2012, Dubai police subjected three British citizens to <a href="/wiki/Battery_(crime)" title="Battery (crime)">beatings</a> and <a href="/wiki/Electric_shocks" class="mw-redirect" title="Electric shocks">electric shocks</a> after arresting them on drugs charges.<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup> The British Prime Minister, <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">David Cameron</a>, expressed "concern" over the case and raised it with the UAE President, Sheikh Khalifa bin Zayed Al Nahyan, during his 2013 state visit to the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup> The three men were pardoned and released in July 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In a report released on 12 July 2018, <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a> urged for 'war crimes' probe on UAE-run prisons in <a href="/wiki/Yemen" title="Yemen">Yemen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">&#91;282&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 10 September 2018, Yemeni detainees in a UAE-run prison underwent a hunger strike to protest their detention. Despite orders by the prosecutors to release some of the detained prisoners, the detainees are still being held.<sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">&#91;283&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Migrant_workers">Migrant workers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Arab_Emirates&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Migrant workers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Migrant_workers_in_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="Migrant workers in the United Arab Emirates">Migrant workers in the United Arab Emirates</a> and <a href="/wiki/Migrant_workers_in_the_Gulf_region" class="mw-redirect" title="Migrant workers in the Gulf region">Migrant workers in the Gulf region</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Burj_Dubai_Construction_Workers_on_25_January_2008_Pict_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Burj_Dubai_Construction_Workers_on_25_January_2008_Pict_2.jpg/220px-Burj_Dubai_Construction_Workers_on_25_January_2008_Pict_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Burj_Dubai_Construction_Workers_on_25_January_2008_Pict_2.jpg/330px-Burj_Dubai_Construction_Workers_on_25_January_2008_Pict_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Burj_Dubai_Construction_Workers_on_25_January_2008_Pict_2.jpg/440px-Burj_Dubai_Construction_Workers_on_25_January_2008_Pict_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1229" data-file-height="848" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Burj_Dubai_Construction_Workers_on_25_January_2008_Pict_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Two south east Asian <a href="/wiki/Blue-collar_workers" class="mw-redirect" title="Blue-collar workers">blue-collar workers</a> posing for a picture with <a href="/wiki/Burj_Khalifa" title="Burj Khalifa">Burj Khalifa</a> on the background.</div></div></div>
<p>Migrant workers are excluded from the UAE's collective labour rights, hence migrants are vulnerable to forced labour. Migrant workers in the UAE are not allowed to join trade unions.<sup id="cite_ref-mig_284-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mig-284">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup> Moreover, migrant workers are banned from going on strike.<sup id="cite_ref-mig_284-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mig-284">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">&#91;285&#93;</a></sup> Dozens of workers were deported in 2014 for going on strike.<sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">&#91;286&#93;</a></sup> As migrant workers do not have the right to join a trade union or go on strike, they don't have the means to denounce the exploitation they suffer. Those who protest risk prison and deportation.<sup id="cite_ref-mig_284-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mig-284">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/International_Trade_Union_Confederation" title="International Trade Union Confederation">International Trade Union Confederation</a> has called on the United Nations to investigate evidence that thousands of migrant workers in the UAE are treated as slave labour.<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">&#91;287&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2013, police arrested a US citizen and some UAE citizens, in connection with a <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> parody video which allegedly portrayed Dubai and its residents in a bad light. The video was shot in areas of <a href="/wiki/Satwa" class="mw-redirect" title="Satwa">Satwa</a>, Dubai, and featured gangs learning how to fight using simple weapons, including shoes, the aghal, etc.<sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288">&#91;288&#93;</a></sup> In 2015, nationals from different countries were put in jail for offences. An Australian woman was accused of 'writing bad words on social media', after she had posted a picture of a vehicle parked illegally. She was later deported from the UAE.<sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The State Security Apparatus in the UAE has been accused of a series of atrocities and human rights abuses including enforced disappearance, arbitrary arrests and torture,<sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">&#91;290&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Freedom of association is also severely curtailed. All associations and NGOs have to register through the Ministry of Social Affairs and are therefore under de facto State control. About twenty non-political groups operate on the territory without registration. All associations have to be submitted to censorship guidelines and all publications have first to be approved by the government.<sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">&#91;291&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dress_code">Dress code</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Arab_Emirates&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Dress code">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The UAE has a modest dress code. The dress code is part of Dubai's criminal law.<sup id="cite_ref-Criminal_Law_of_Dubai_292-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Criminal_Law_of_Dubai-292">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup> Most malls in the UAE have a dress code displayed at entrances.<sup id="cite_ref-code_293-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-code-293">&#91;293&#93;</a></sup> At Dubai's malls, women are encouraged to cover their shoulders and knees.<sup id="cite_ref-code_293-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-code-293">&#91;293&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-modest_294-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-modest-294">&#91;294&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Dubai_Mall_dress_code_295-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dubai_Mall_dress_code-295">&#91;295&#93;</a></sup> But people can wear swimwear at the pools and beaches.
</p><p>People are also requested to wear modest clothing when entering mosques, such as the <a href="/wiki/Sheikh_Zayed_Mosque" title="Sheikh Zayed Mosque">Sheikh Zayed Mosque</a> in Abu Dhabi. Mosques which are open to tourists provide modest clothing for men and women if needed.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Arab_Emirates&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The UAE's <a href="/wiki/Media_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="Media of the United Arab Emirates">media</a> is annually classified as "not free" in the <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_the_Press_(report)" title="Freedom of the Press (report)">Freedom of the Press</a> report by <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296">&#91;296&#93;</a></sup> The UAE ranks poorly in the annual <a href="/wiki/Press_Freedom_Index" title="Press Freedom Index">Press Freedom Index</a> by <a href="/wiki/Reporters_without_Borders" class="mw-redirect" title="Reporters without Borders">Reporters without Borders</a>. <a href="/wiki/Dubai_Media_City" title="Dubai Media City">Dubai Media City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Twofour54" title="Twofour54">twofour54</a> are the UAE's main media zones. The UAE is home to some pan-Arab broadcasters, including the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East_Broadcasting_Centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Middle East Broadcasting Centre">Middle East Broadcasting Centre</a> and <a href="/wiki/Orbit_Showtime_Network" class="mw-redirect" title="Orbit Showtime Network">Orbit Showtime Network</a>. In 2007, Sheikh <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_bin_Rashid_Al_Maktoum" title="Mohammed bin Rashid Al Maktoum">Mohammed bin Rashid Al Maktoum</a> decreed that journalists can no longer be prosecuted or imprisoned for reasons relating to their work.<sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">&#91;297&#93;</a></sup> At the same time, the UAE has made it illegal to disseminate online material that can threaten "public order".<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">&#91;298&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Criticism of the government is not allowed. Criticism of government officials and royal family members is not allowed. Prison terms have been given to those who "deride or damage" the reputation of the state and "display contempt" for religion.<sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299">&#91;299&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Arab_Emirates&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="Economy of the United Arab Emirates">Economy of the United Arab Emirates</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dubai_Marina_Beach_Panorama.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Dubai_Marina_Beach_Panorama.jpg/220px-Dubai_Marina_Beach_Panorama.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="89" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Dubai_Marina_Beach_Panorama.jpg/330px-Dubai_Marina_Beach_Panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Dubai_Marina_Beach_Panorama.jpg/440px-Dubai_Marina_Beach_Panorama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4832" data-file-height="1944" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dubai_Marina_Beach_Panorama.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Dubai_Marina" title="Dubai Marina">Dubai Marina</a> Beach</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Burj_Khalifa.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/93/Burj_Khalifa.jpg/170px-Burj_Khalifa.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="298" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/93/Burj_Khalifa.jpg/255px-Burj_Khalifa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/93/Burj_Khalifa.jpg/340px-Burj_Khalifa.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3279" data-file-height="5740" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Burj_Khalifa.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Burj_Khalifa" title="Burj Khalifa">Burj Khalifa</a> is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_and_structures_in_the_world" class="mw-redirect" title="List of tallest buildings and structures in the world">tallest man-made structure in the world</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Abu_dhabi_skylines_2014.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Abu_dhabi_skylines_2014.jpg/220px-Abu_dhabi_skylines_2014.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="121" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Abu_dhabi_skylines_2014.jpg/330px-Abu_dhabi_skylines_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Abu_dhabi_skylines_2014.jpg/440px-Abu_dhabi_skylines_2014.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5726" data-file-height="3143" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Abu_dhabi_skylines_2014.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Abu Dhabi skyline</div></div></div>
<p>UAE has the second largest economy in the GCC (after Saudi Arabia),<sup id="cite_ref-Economy2013_300-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Economy2013-300">&#91;300&#93;</a></sup> with a gross domestic product (GDP) of $377 billion (1.38 trillion AED) in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-GDP2012_301-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GDP2012-301">&#91;301&#93;</a></sup> Since independence in 1971, UAE's economy has grown by nearly 231 times to 1.45 trillion AED in 2013. The non-oil trade has grown to 1.2 trillion AED, a growth by around 28 times from 1981 to 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-Economy2013_300-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Economy2013-300">&#91;300&#93;</a></sup> UAE is ranked as the 26th best nation in the world for doing business based on its economy and regulatory environment, ranked by the <a href="/wiki/Doing_Business_Report" class="mw-redirect" title="Doing Business Report">Doing Business 2017 Report</a> published by the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank_Group" title="World Bank Group">World Bank Group</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Doing_Business_302-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Doing_Business-302">&#91;302&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Although UAE has the most diversified economy in the GCC, the UAE's economy remains extremely reliant on oil. With the exception of Dubai, most of the UAE is dependent on oil revenues. Petroleum and natural gas continue to play a central role in the economy, especially in <a href="/wiki/Abu_Dhabi" title="Abu Dhabi">Abu Dhabi</a>. More than 85% of the UAE's economy was based on the oil exports in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-WTO_Trade_Statistic_2009_303-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WTO_Trade_Statistic_2009-303">&#91;303&#93;</a></sup> While Abu Dhabi and other UAE emirates have remained relatively conservative in their approach to diversification, Dubai, which has far smaller oil reserves, was bolder in its diversification policy.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc.co.uk_16-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc.co.uk-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, oil exports accounted for 77% of the UAE's state budget.<sup id="cite_ref-lse.ac.uk_304-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lse.ac.uk-304">&#91;304&#93;</a></sup> Successful efforts at economic diversification have reduced the portion of GDP based on oil/gas output to 25%.<sup id="cite_ref-WorldFactbook_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WorldFactbook-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
Dubai suffered from a significant economic crisis in 2007–2010 and was bailed out by Abu Dhabi's oil wealth.<sup id="cite_ref-Speaking_of_Water_305-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Speaking_of_Water-305">&#91;305&#93;</a></sup> Dubai is running a balanced budget, reflecting economic growth.<sup id="cite_ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306">&#91;306&#93;</a></sup> Tourism acts as a growth sector for the entire UAE economy. Dubai is the top tourism destination in the Middle East.<sup id="cite_ref-tdb_203-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tdb-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> According to the annual MasterCard Global Destination Cities Index, Dubai is the fifth most popular tourism destination in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307">&#91;307&#93;</a></sup> Dubai holds up to 66% share of the UAE's tourism economy, with Abu Dhabi having 16% and Sharjah 10%. Dubai welcomed 10 million tourists in 2013.
The UAE has the most advanced and developed infrastructure in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-308" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-308">&#91;308&#93;</a></sup> Since the 1980s, the UAE has been spending billions of dollars on infrastructure. These developments are particularly evident in the larger emirates of Abu Dhabi and Dubai. The northern emirates are rapidly following suit, providing major incentives for developers of residential and commercial property.<sup id="cite_ref-309" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-309">&#91;309&#93;</a></sup>
Property prices in Dubai fell dramatically when <a href="/wiki/Dubai_World" title="Dubai World">Dubai World</a>, the government construction company, sought to delay a debt payment.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>UAE law does not allow trade unions to exist.<sup id="cite_ref-ituc_310-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ituc-310">&#91;310&#93;</a></sup> The right to <a href="/wiki/Collective_bargaining" title="Collective bargaining">collective bargaining</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Right_to_strike" class="mw-redirect" title="Right to strike">right to strike</a> are not recognised, and the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Labour" title="Ministry of Labour">Ministry of Labour</a> has the power to force workers to go back to work. Migrant workers who participate in a strike can have their work permits cancelled and be deported.<sup id="cite_ref-ituc_310-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ituc-310">&#91;310&#93;</a></sup> Consequently, there are very few anti-discrimination laws in relation to labour issues, with Emiratis – other <a href="/wiki/Cooperation_Council_for_the_Arab_States_of_the_Gulf" class="mw-redirect" title="Cooperation Council for the Arab States of the Gulf">GCC</a> Arabs – getting preference in public sector jobs despite lesser credentials than competitors and lower motivation. In fact, just over eighty percent of Emirati workers hold government posts, with many of the rest taking part in state-owned enterprises such as <a href="/wiki/Emirates_(airline)" title="Emirates (airline)">Emirates airlines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dubai_Properties" title="Dubai Properties">Dubai Properties</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-311" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-311">&#91;311&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Arab_Emirates&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r889293853/mw-parser-output/.tmulti"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:408px;max-width:408px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:192px;max-width:192px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Emirates_Airbus_A380_(A6-EDS)_departs_London_Heathrow_11April2015.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Emirates_Airbus_A380_%28A6-EDS%29_departs_London_Heathrow_11April2015.jpg/190px-Emirates_Airbus_A380_%28A6-EDS%29_departs_London_Heathrow_11April2015.jpg" decoding="async" width="190" height="139" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Emirates_Airbus_A380_%28A6-EDS%29_departs_London_Heathrow_11April2015.jpg/285px-Emirates_Airbus_A380_%28A6-EDS%29_departs_London_Heathrow_11April2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Emirates_Airbus_A380_%28A6-EDS%29_departs_London_Heathrow_11April2015.jpg/380px-Emirates_Airbus_A380_%28A6-EDS%29_departs_London_Heathrow_11April2015.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4653" data-file-height="3401" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Emirates_(airline)" title="Emirates (airline)">Emirates</a>, one of the world's largest airlines based in <a href="/wiki/Dubai" title="Dubai">Dubai</a>.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:212px;max-width:212px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Etihad_Airways_-_Airbus_A380-861.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Etihad_Airways_-_Airbus_A380-861.jpg/210px-Etihad_Airways_-_Airbus_A380-861.jpg" decoding="async" width="210" height="140" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Etihad_Airways_-_Airbus_A380-861.jpg/315px-Etihad_Airways_-_Airbus_A380-861.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Etihad_Airways_-_Airbus_A380-861.jpg/420px-Etihad_Airways_-_Airbus_A380-861.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Etihad_Airways" title="Etihad Airways">Etihad Airways</a>, second largest airline in UAE based in <a href="/wiki/Abu_Dhabi" title="Abu Dhabi">Abu Dhabi</a>.</div></div></div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="Transport in the United Arab Emirates">Transport in the United Arab Emirates</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Dubai_International_Airport" title="Dubai International Airport">Dubai International Airport</a> was the <a href="/wiki/World%27s_busiest_airports_by_international_passenger_traffic" class="mw-redirect" title="World&#39;s busiest airports by international passenger traffic">busiest airport in the world by international passenger traffic</a> in 2014, overtaking London Heathrow.<sup id="cite_ref-312" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-312">&#91;312&#93;</a></sup> A 1,200&#160;km (750&#160;mi) <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="Rail transport in the United Arab Emirates">country-wide railway</a> is under construction which will connect all the major cities and ports.<sup id="cite_ref-IRJMar12_313-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IRJMar12-313">&#91;313&#93;</a></sup> The Dubai Metro is the first urban train network in the Arabian Peninsula.<sup id="cite_ref-314" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-314">&#91;314&#93;</a></sup> The major ports of the United Arab Emirates are <a href="/wiki/Khalifa_Port" title="Khalifa Port">Khalifa Port</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zayed_Port" title="Zayed Port">Zayed Port</a>, Port <a href="/wiki/Jebel_Ali" title="Jebel Ali">Jebel Ali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Port_Rashid" title="Port Rashid">Port Rashid</a>, Port Khalid, <a href="/wiki/Port_Saeed" title="Port Saeed">Port Saeed</a>, and Port Khor Fakkan.<sup id="cite_ref-315" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-315">&#91;315&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Abu Dhabi, Dubai, Sharjah, Ajman, Umm Al Quwain, and Ras Al Khaimah are connected by the <a href="/wiki/E_11_road_(United_Arab_Emirates)" title="E 11 road (United Arab Emirates)">E11 highway</a>, which is the longest road in the UAE. In Dubai, in addition to the metro, <a href="/wiki/Dubai_Tram" title="Dubai Tram">Dubai Tram</a> and <a href="/wiki/Palm_Jumeirah_Monorail" title="Palm Jumeirah Monorail">Palm Jumeirah Monorail</a> also connect specific parts of the city.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Telecommunications">Telecommunications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Arab_Emirates&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Telecommunications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The UAE is served by two telecommunications operators, <a href="/wiki/Etisalat" title="Etisalat">Etisalat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Emirates_Integrated_Telecommunications_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Emirates Integrated Telecommunications Company">Emirates Integrated Telecommunications Company</a> ("du"). Etisalat operated a monopoly until du launched mobile services in February 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-etisalatmon_316-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-etisalatmon-316">&#91;316&#93;</a></sup> Internet subscribers were expected to increase from 0.904 million in 2007 to 2.66 million in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-317" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-317">&#91;317&#93;</a></sup> The regulator, the Telecommunications Regulatory Authority, mandates filtering websites for religious, political and sexual content.<sup id="cite_ref-318" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-318">&#91;318&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/5G" title="5G">5G</a> wireless services were installed nationwide in 2019 through a partnership with <a href="/wiki/Huawei" title="Huawei">Huawei</a><sup id="cite_ref-319" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-319">&#91;319&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Arab_Emirates&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="Culture of the United Arab Emirates">Culture of the United Arab Emirates</a></div><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Emirati_Dialect" title="Emirati Dialect">Emirati Dialect</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Deira_Souk_on_9_May_2007_Pict_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Deira_Souk_on_9_May_2007_Pict_2.jpg/220px-Deira_Souk_on_9_May_2007_Pict_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="134" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Deira_Souk_on_9_May_2007_Pict_2.jpg/330px-Deira_Souk_on_9_May_2007_Pict_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Deira_Souk_on_9_May_2007_Pict_2.jpg/440px-Deira_Souk_on_9_May_2007_Pict_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1037" data-file-height="630" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Deira_Souk_on_9_May_2007_Pict_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A traditional <i><a href="/wiki/Souq" title="Souq">souk</a></i> in <a href="/wiki/Deira,_Dubai" title="Deira, Dubai">Deira</a>, Dubai</div></div></div>
<p>Emirati culture is based on <a href="/wiki/Arabian_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabian culture">Arabian culture</a> and has been influenced by the cultures of Persia, India, and East Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-folk_320-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-folk-320">&#91;320&#93;</a></sup> Arabian and <a href="/wiki/Persian_architecture" class="mw-redirect" title="Persian architecture">Persian inspired architecture</a> is part of the expression of the local Emirati identity.<sup id="cite_ref-loc_321-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loc-321">&#91;321&#93;</a></sup> Persian influence on Emirati culture is noticeably visible in traditional Emirati architecture and <a href="/wiki/Folk_arts" title="Folk arts">folk arts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-folk_320-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-folk-320">&#91;320&#93;</a></sup> For example, the distinctive wind tower which tops traditional Emirati buildings, the <i><a href="/wiki/Barjeel" class="mw-redirect" title="Barjeel">barjeel</a></i> has become an identifying mark of Emirati architecture and is attributed to Persian influence.<sup id="cite_ref-folk_320-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-folk-320">&#91;320&#93;</a></sup> This influence is derived both from traders who fled the tax regime in Persia in the early 19th Century and from Emirati ownership of ports on the Persian coast, for instance the Al Qassimi port of Lingeh.<sup id="cite_ref-322" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-322">&#91;322&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Haribya_Band.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Haribya_Band.jpg/220px-Haribya_Band.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Haribya_Band.jpg/330px-Haribya_Band.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Haribya_Band.jpg/440px-Haribya_Band.jpg 2x" data-file-width="964" data-file-height="715" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Haribya_Band.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A band performs a razfah in an Emirati wedding. Razfah is a cultural dance derived from Arab tribes sword battles.</div></div></div>
<p>The United Arab Emirates has a diverse society.<sup id="cite_ref-migrationinformation_323-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-migrationinformation-323">&#91;323&#93;</a></sup> Major holidays in the United Arab Emirates include <i><a href="/wiki/Eid_ul-Fitr" class="mw-redirect" title="Eid ul-Fitr">Eid al Fitr</a></i>, which marks the end of <i><a href="/wiki/Ramadan" title="Ramadan">Ramadan</a></i>, and <a href="/wiki/National_Day_(United_Arab_Emirates)" title="National Day (United Arab Emirates)">National Day</a> (2 December), which marks the formation of the United Arab Emirates.<sup id="cite_ref-324" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-324">&#91;324&#93;</a></sup> Emirati males prefer to wear a <a href="/wiki/Thawb" title="Thawb">kandura</a>, an ankle-length white tunic woven from wool or cotton, and Emirati women wear an <a href="/wiki/Abaya" title="Abaya">abaya</a>, a black over-garment that covers most parts of the body.<sup id="cite_ref-325" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-325">&#91;325&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Ancient Emirati poetry was strongly influenced by the 8th-century Arab scholar Al Khalil bin Ahmed. The earliest known poet in the UAE is <a href="/wiki/Ibn_Majid" class="mw-redirect" title="Ibn Majid">Ibn Majid</a>, born between 1432 and 1437 in Ras Al-Khaimah. The most famous Emirati writers were Mubarak Al Oqaili (1880–1954), Salem bin Ali al Owais (1887–1959) and Ahmed bin Sulayem (1905–1976). Three other poets from Sharjah, known as the Hirah group, are observed to have been heavily influenced by the Apollo and <a href="/wiki/Romantic_poetry" title="Romantic poetry">Romantic poets</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-poetry_326-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-poetry-326">&#91;326&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Sharjah_International_Book_Fair" title="Sharjah International Book Fair">Sharjah International Book Fair</a> is the oldest and largest in the country.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/List_of_museums_in_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="List of museums in the United Arab Emirates">list of museums in the United Arab Emirates</a> includes some of regional repute, most famously <a href="/wiki/Sharjah_(city)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sharjah (city)">Sharjah</a> with its Heritage District containing 17 museums,<sup id="cite_ref-327" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-327">&#91;327&#93;</a></sup> which in 1998 was the Cultural Capital of the Arab World.<sup id="cite_ref-328" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-328">&#91;328&#93;</a></sup> In Dubai, the area of <a href="/wiki/Al_Quoz" title="Al Quoz">Al Quoz</a> has attracted a number of art galleries as well as museums such as the <a href="/wiki/Salsali_Private_Museum" title="Salsali Private Museum">Salsali Private Museum</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-329" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-329">&#91;329&#93;</a></sup> Abu Dhabi has established a culture district on <a href="/wiki/Saadiyat_Island" title="Saadiyat Island">Saadiyat Island</a>. Six grand projects are planned, including the <a href="/wiki/Guggenheim_Abu_Dhabi" title="Guggenheim Abu Dhabi">Guggenheim Abu Dhabi</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Louvre_Abu_Dhabi" title="Louvre Abu Dhabi">Louvre Abu Dhabi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-330" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-330">&#91;330&#93;</a></sup> Dubai also plans to build a <a href="/wiki/Kunsthal" title="Kunsthal">Kunsthal</a> museum and a district for galleries and artists.<sup id="cite_ref-331" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-331">&#91;331&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Emirati culture is a part of the <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Eastern_Arabia" title="Culture of Eastern Arabia">culture of Eastern Arabia</a>. <a href="/wiki/Liwa_(music)" title="Liwa (music)">Liwa</a> is a type of music and dance performed locally, mainly in communities that contain descendants of <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantu peoples</a> from the <a href="/wiki/African_Great_Lakes" title="African Great Lakes">African Great Lakes</a> region.<sup id="cite_ref-poetry_326-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-poetry-326">&#91;326&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Dubai_Desert_Rock_Festival" title="Dubai Desert Rock Festival">Dubai Desert Rock Festival</a> is also another major festival consisting of heavy metal and rock artists.<sup id="cite_ref-332" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-332">&#91;332&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="Cinema of the United Arab Emirates">cinema of the United Arab Emirates</a> is minimal but expanding.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Arab_Emirates&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Emirati_cuisine" title="Emirati cuisine">Emirati cuisine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Luqaimat.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Luqaimat.jpg/220px-Luqaimat.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Luqaimat.jpg/330px-Luqaimat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Luqaimat.jpg/440px-Luqaimat.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1075" data-file-height="1074" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Luqaimat.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Arabic_coffee" title="Arabic coffee">Arabic coffee</a> with <a href="/wiki/Lugaimat" class="mw-redirect" title="Lugaimat">Lugaimat</a>; a traditional Emirati sweet.</div></div></div>
<p>The traditional food of the Emirates has always been rice, fish and meat. The people of the United Arab Emirates have adopted most of their foods from other West and South Asian countries including Iran, Saudi Arabia, Pakistan, India and Oman. Seafood has been the mainstay of the Emirati diet for centuries. Meat and rice are other staple foods, with <a href="/wiki/Lamb_and_mutton" title="Lamb and mutton">lamb and mutton</a> preferred to goat and beef. Popular beverages are coffee and tea, which can be complemented with <a href="/wiki/Cardamom" title="Cardamom">cardamom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saffron" title="Saffron">saffron</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Spearmint" title="Spearmint">mint</a> to give them a distinctive flavour.<sup id="cite_ref-333" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-333">&#91;333&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Popular cultural Emirati dishes include <i>threed</i>, <i>machboos</i>, <i>khubisa</i>, <i>khameer</i> and <i>chabab</i> bread among others while <a href="/wiki/Lugaimat" class="mw-redirect" title="Lugaimat">Lugaimat</a> is a famous Emirati dessert.
</p><p>With the influence of western culture, fast food has become very popular among young people, to the extent that campaigns have been held to highlight the dangers of fast food excesses.<sup id="cite_ref-334" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-334">&#91;334&#93;</a></sup> Alcohol is allowed to be served only in hotel restaurants and bars. All nightclubs are permitted to sell alcohol. Specific supermarkets may sell alcohol, but these products are sold in separate sections. Likewise, pork, which is <a href="/wiki/Haram" title="Haram">haram</a> (not permitted for Muslims), is sold in separate sections in all major supermarkets. Note that although alcohol may be consumed, it is illegal to be intoxicated in public or drive a motor vehicle with any trace of alcohol in the blood.<sup id="cite_ref-335" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-335">&#91;335&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Arab_Emirates&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="Sport in the United Arab Emirates">Sport in the United Arab Emirates</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Yas_Marina_Circuit,_October_12,_2018_SkySat_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Yas_Marina_Circuit%2C_October_12%2C_2018_SkySat_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Yas_Marina_Circuit%2C_October_12%2C_2018_SkySat_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Yas_Marina_Circuit%2C_October_12%2C_2018_SkySat_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Yas_Marina_Circuit%2C_October_12%2C_2018_SkySat_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Yas_Marina_Circuit%2C_October_12%2C_2018_SkySat_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Yas_Marina_Circuit%2C_October_12%2C_2018_SkySat_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2542" data-file-height="1430" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Yas_Marina_Circuit,_October_12,_2018_SkySat_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Yas_Marina_Circuit" title="Yas Marina Circuit">Yas Marina Circuit</a> in <a href="/wiki/Abu_Dhabi" title="Abu Dhabi">Abu Dhabi</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:DTC1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/DTC1.jpg/220px-DTC1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/DTC1.jpg/330px-DTC1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/DTC1.jpg/440px-DTC1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="545" data-file-height="409" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:DTC1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Dubai_Tennis_Championships" title="Dubai Tennis Championships">Dubai Tennis Championships</a> in 2006</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">Formula One</a> is particularly popular in the United Arab Emirates, and is annually held at the <a href="/wiki/Yas_Marina_Circuit" title="Yas Marina Circuit">Yas Marina Circuit</a>. The race takes place in the evening, and was the first ever Grand Prix to start in daylight and finish at night.<sup id="cite_ref-336" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-336">&#91;336&#93;</a></sup> Other popular sports include <a href="/wiki/Camel_racing" title="Camel racing">camel racing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Falconry" title="Falconry">falconry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Endurance_riding" title="Endurance riding">endurance riding</a>, and tennis.<sup id="cite_ref-337" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-337">&#91;337&#93;</a></sup> The emirate of Dubai is also home to two major golf courses: The Dubai Golf Club and <a href="/wiki/Emirates_Golf_Club" title="Emirates Golf Club">Emirates Golf Club</a>.
</p><p>In the past, child camel jockeys were used, leading to widespread criticism. Eventually the UAE passed laws banning the use of children for the sport, leading to the prompt removal of almost all child jockeys.<sup id="cite_ref-338" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-338">&#91;338&#93;</a></sup> Recently robot jockeys have been introduced to overcome the problem of child camel jockeys which was an issue of human right violations. <a href="/wiki/Ansar_Burney" title="Ansar Burney">Ansar Burney</a> is often praised for the work he has done in this area.<sup id="cite_ref-339" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-339">&#91;339&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Arab_Emirates&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> is a popular sport in the UAE. <a href="/wiki/Al-Nasr_Dubai_SC" title="Al-Nasr Dubai SC">Al Nasr</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Ain_Club" class="mw-redirect" title="Al Ain Club">Al Ain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Wasl_FC" class="mw-redirect" title="Al Wasl FC">Al Wasl</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sharjah_FC" title="Sharjah FC">Sharjah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Wahda_FC" title="Al Wahda FC">Al Wahda</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Shabab_Al-Ahli_Dubai_FC" title="Shabab Al-Ahli Dubai FC">Shabab Al Ahli</a> are the most popular teams and enjoy the reputation of long-time regional champions.<sup id="cite_ref-340" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-340">&#91;340&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates_Football_Association" title="United Arab Emirates Football Association">United Arab Emirates Football Association</a> was established in 1971 and since then has dedicated its time and effort to promoting the game, organising <a href="/wiki/Youth_program" title="Youth program">youth programmes</a> and improving the abilities of not only its players, but also the officials and coaches involved with its regional teams. The <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates_national_football_team" title="United Arab Emirates national football team">UAE</a> qualified for the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a> in <a href="/wiki/1990_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1990 FIFA World Cup">1990</a>, along with <a href="/wiki/Egypt_national_football_team" title="Egypt national football team">Egypt</a>. It was the third consecutive World Cup with two Arab nations qualifying, after <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_national_football_team" title="Kuwait national football team">Kuwait</a> and <a href="/wiki/Algeria_national_football_team" title="Algeria national football team">Algeria</a> in <a href="/wiki/1982_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1982 FIFA World Cup">1982</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Iraq_national_football_team" title="Iraq national football team">Iraq</a> and Algeria again in <a href="/wiki/1986_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1986 FIFA World Cup">1986</a>. The UAE has won the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Cup_of_Nations" class="mw-redirect" title="Gulf Cup of Nations">Gulf Cup Championship</a> twice: the first cup won in January 2007 held in <a href="/wiki/Abu_Dhabi" title="Abu Dhabi">Abu Dhabi</a> and the second in January 2013, held in Bahrain.<sup id="cite_ref-341" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-341">&#91;341&#93;</a></sup> The country hosted the <a href="/wiki/2019_AFC_Asian_Cup" title="2019 AFC Asian Cup">2019 AFC Asian Cup</a>. The UAE team went all the way to the semi-finals, where they were defeated by the eventual champions, <a href="/wiki/Qatar_national_football_team" title="Qatar national football team">Qatar.</a>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cricket">Cricket</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Arab_Emirates&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Cricket">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">Cricket</a> is one of the most popular sports in the UAE, largely because of the expatriate population from the <a href="/wiki/SAARC" class="mw-redirect" title="SAARC">SAARC</a> countries, the United Kingdom, and Australia. The <a href="/wiki/Sharjah_Cricket_Association_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Sharjah Cricket Association Stadium">Sharjah Cricket Association Stadium</a> in Sharjah has hosted four international <a href="/wiki/Test_cricket" title="Test cricket">test cricket matches</a> so far.<sup id="cite_ref-342" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-342">&#91;342&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sheikh_Zayed_Cricket_Stadium" title="Sheikh Zayed Cricket Stadium">Sheikh Zayed Cricket Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Abu_Dhabi" title="Abu Dhabi">Abu Dhabi</a> has also hosted <a href="/wiki/International_structure_of_cricket" class="mw-redirect" title="International structure of cricket">international cricket</a> matches. Dubai has two cricket stadiums (Dubai <a href="/wiki/Cricket_field" title="Cricket field">Cricket Ground</a> No. 1 and No. 2) with a third, the <a href="/wiki/DSC_Cricket_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="DSC Cricket Stadium">DSC Cricket Stadium</a>, as part of <a href="/wiki/Dubai_Sports_City" title="Dubai Sports City">Dubai Sports City</a>. Dubai is also home to the <a href="/wiki/International_Cricket_Council" title="International Cricket Council">International Cricket Council</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-343" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-343">&#91;343&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates_national_cricket_team" title="United Arab Emirates national cricket team">UAE national cricket team</a> qualified for the <a href="/wiki/1996_Cricket_World_Cup" title="1996 Cricket World Cup">1996 Cricket World Cup</a> and narrowly missed out on qualification for the <a href="/wiki/2007_Cricket_World_Cup" title="2007 Cricket World Cup">2007 Cricket World Cup</a>. They qualified for the <a href="/wiki/2015_Cricket_World_Cup" title="2015 Cricket World Cup">2015 Cricket World Cup</a> held in Australia and New Zealand.<sup id="cite_ref-344" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-344">&#91;344&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-345" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-345">&#91;345&#93;</a></sup> The 14th edition of the <a href="/wiki/2018_Asia_Cup" title="2018 Asia Cup">Asia Cup</a> Cricket tournament was held in the UAE in September 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-346" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-346">&#91;346&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Arab_Emirates&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="Education in the United Arab Emirates">Education in the United Arab Emirates</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:UniversityCityHall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/UniversityCityHall.jpg/220px-UniversityCityHall.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/UniversityCityHall.jpg/330px-UniversityCityHall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/UniversityCityHall.jpg/440px-UniversityCityHall.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:UniversityCityHall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>University City Hall is the largest hall located in <a href="/wiki/Sharjah_University_City" class="mw-redirect" title="Sharjah University City">University City</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sharjah" title="Sharjah">Sharjah</a>. Graduation ceremonies  of <a href="/wiki/American_University_of_Sharjah" title="American University of Sharjah">American University of Sharjah</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Sharjah" title="University of Sharjah">University of Sharjah</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Higher_Colleges_of_Technology" title="Higher Colleges of Technology">Higher Colleges of Technology</a> are notably held here.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Abu_Dhabi_University_2013_03_13_(8582695329).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Abu_Dhabi_University_2013_03_13_%288582695329%29.jpg/220px-Abu_Dhabi_University_2013_03_13_%288582695329%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Abu_Dhabi_University_2013_03_13_%288582695329%29.jpg/330px-Abu_Dhabi_University_2013_03_13_%288582695329%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Abu_Dhabi_University_2013_03_13_%288582695329%29.jpg/440px-Abu_Dhabi_University_2013_03_13_%288582695329%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4752" data-file-height="3168" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Abu_Dhabi_University_2013_03_13_(8582695329).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Abu_Dhabi_University" title="Abu Dhabi University">Abu Dhabi University</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Education" title="Education">education system</a> through secondary level is monitored by the Ministry of Education in all emirates except Abu Dhabi, where it falls under the authority of the <a href="/wiki/Abu_Dhabi_Education_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Abu Dhabi Education Council">Abu Dhabi Education Council</a>. It consists of primary schools, <a href="/wiki/Middle_school" title="Middle school">middle schools</a> and high schools. The public schools are government-funded and the curriculum is created to match the United Arab Emirates' development goals. The medium of instruction in the public school is Arabic with emphasis on English as a second language. There are also many private schools which are internationally accredited. <a href="/wiki/Public_school_(government_funded)" class="mw-redirect" title="Public school (government funded)">Public schools</a> in the country are free for citizens of the UAE, while the fees for private schools vary.
</p><p>The higher education system is monitored by the Ministry of Higher Education. The ministry also is responsible for admitting students to its <a href="/wiki/Undergraduate_education" title="Undergraduate education">undergraduate</a> institutions.<sup id="cite_ref-347" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-347">&#91;347&#93;</a></sup> The adult literacy rate in 2011 was 90%.<sup id="cite_ref-348" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-348">&#91;348&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="collection doesn&#39;t include any Country Studies for UAE (December 2015)">failed verification</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-349" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-349">&#91;349&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="website gives literacy rates for some countries but not UAE (December 2015)">failed verification</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-undata201512_350-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-undata201512-350">&#91;350&#93;</a></sup> Thousands of nationals are pursuing formal learning at 86 <a href="/wiki/Adult_education" title="Adult education">adult education</a> centres spread across the country.<sup id="cite_ref-351" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-351">&#91;351&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The UAE has shown a strong interest in improving education and research. Enterprises include the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/CERT_Group_of_Companies" title="CERT Group of Companies">CERT</a> Research Centers and the <a href="/wiki/Masdar_Institute_of_Science_and_Technology" title="Masdar Institute of Science and Technology">Masdar Institute of Science and Technology</a> and Institute for Enterprise Development.<sup id="cite_ref-352" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-352">&#91;352&#93;</a></sup> According to the QS Rankings, the top-ranking universities in the country are the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates_University" title="United Arab Emirates University">United Arab Emirates University</a> (421–430th worldwide), <a href="/wiki/Khalifa_University" title="Khalifa University">Khalifa University</a><sup id="cite_ref-353" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-353">&#91;353&#93;</a></sup> (441–450th worldwide), the <a href="/wiki/American_University_of_Sharjah" title="American University of Sharjah">American University of Sharjah</a> (431–440th) and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Sharjah" title="University of Sharjah">University of Sharjah</a> (551–600th worldwide).<sup id="cite_ref-354" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-354">&#91;354&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Arab_Emirates&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="Demographics of the United Arab Emirates">Demographics of the United Arab Emirates</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Palm_jumeirah_core.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Palm_jumeirah_core.jpg/220px-Palm_jumeirah_core.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Palm_jumeirah_core.jpg/330px-Palm_jumeirah_core.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Palm_jumeirah_core.jpg/440px-Palm_jumeirah_core.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="857" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Palm_jumeirah_core.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Residential villas in the <a href="/wiki/Palm_Jumeirah" title="Palm Jumeirah">Palm Jumeirah</a> palm fronds in <a href="/wiki/Dubai" title="Dubai">Dubai</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sharjah,_UAE.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Sharjah%2C_UAE.jpg/220px-Sharjah%2C_UAE.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Sharjah%2C_UAE.jpg/330px-Sharjah%2C_UAE.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Sharjah%2C_UAE.jpg/440px-Sharjah%2C_UAE.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sharjah,_UAE.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The old residential area in <a href="/wiki/Sharjah" title="Sharjah">Sharjah</a>, displaying local architecture.</div></div></div>
<p>According to an estimate by the World Bank, the UAE's population in 2018 stands at 9.543 million. Expatriates and immigrants account for 88.52% while Emiratis make up the remaining 11.48%.<sup id="cite_ref-355" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-355">&#91;355&#93;</a></sup> This unique imbalance is due to the country's exceptionally high <a href="/wiki/Net_migration_rate" title="Net migration rate">net migration rate</a> of 21.71, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_net_migration_rate" title="List of countries by net migration rate">world's highest</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-356" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-356">&#91;356&#93;</a></sup> Under Article 8 of UAE Federal Law No. 17, an expatriate can apply for <a href="/wiki/Emirati_nationality_law" title="Emirati nationality law">UAE citizenship</a> after residing in the country for 20 years, providing they have never been convicted of a crime and can speak fluent <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">Arabic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-357" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-357">&#91;357&#93;</a></sup> Only 1.4 million inhabitants are citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-natur_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-natur-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The UAE is ethnically diverse. The five most populous nationalities in the emirates of Dubai, Sharjah, and Ajman are Indian (11%), Pakistani (10%), Emirati (40%), Bangladeshi (7%), and Filipino (6%).<sup id="cite_ref-358" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-358">&#91;358&#93;</a></sup>  Expatriates from Europe, Australia, Northern America and Latin America make up 500,000 of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-arabianbusiness.com_359-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arabianbusiness.com-359">&#91;359&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-360" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-360">&#91;360&#93;</a></sup> More than 100,000 British nationals live in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-361" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-361">&#91;361&#93;</a></sup> The rest of the population are from other <a href="/wiki/Arab_World" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab World">Arab states</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WorldFactbook_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WorldFactbook-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-362" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-362">&#91;362&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>About 88% of the population of the United Arab Emirates is urban.<sup id="cite_ref-363" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-363">&#91;363&#93;</a></sup> The average <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_life_expectancy" title="List of countries by life expectancy">life expectancy</a> was 76.7 in 2012, higher than for any other Arab country.<sup id="cite_ref-364" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-364">&#91;364&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-uaeinteract2_365-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uaeinteract2-365">&#91;365&#93;</a></sup> With a male/female <a href="/wiki/Human_sex_ratio" title="Human sex ratio">sex ratio</a> of 2.2 males for each female in the total population and 2.75 to 1 for the 15–65 <a href="/wiki/Demographic_profile" title="Demographic profile">age group</a>, the UAE's <a href="/wiki/Gender_mortality_differentials" class="mw-redirect" title="Gender mortality differentials">gender imbalance</a> is second highest in the world after Qatar.<sup id="cite_ref-366" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-366">&#91;366&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Arab_Emirates&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="Religion in the United Arab Emirates">Religion in the United Arab Emirates</a></div>
<div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;">
