</tbody></table>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> is the largest and the official <a href="/wiki/State_religion" title="State religion">state religion</a> of the UAE. The government follows a policy of tolerance toward other religions and rarely interferes in the activities of non-Muslims.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_369-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-369">&#91;369&#93;</a></sup> By the same token, non-Muslims are expected to avoid interfering in Islamic religious matters or the Islamic upbringing of Muslims.
</p><p>The government imposes restrictions on spreading other religions through any form of media as it is considered a form of <a href="/wiki/Proselytism" title="Proselytism">proselytizing</a>. There are approximately 31 churches throughout the country, one Hindu temple in the region of <a href="/wiki/Bur_Dubai" title="Bur Dubai">Bur Dubai</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-370" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-370">&#91;370&#93;</a></sup> one Sikh Gurudwara in Jebel Ali and also a Buddhist temple in Al Garhoud.
</p><p>Based on the Ministry of Economy census in 2005, 76% of the total population was <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslim</a>, 13% Christian, and 11% other (mainly <a href="/wiki/Hindu" class="mw-redirect" title="Hindu">Hindu</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-religiousfreedom_209-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-religiousfreedom-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> Census figures do not take into account the many "temporary" visitors and workers while also counting <a href="/wiki/Baha%27is" class="mw-redirect" title="Baha&#39;is">Baha'is</a> and <a href="/wiki/Druze" title="Druze">Druze</a> as Muslim.<sup id="cite_ref-religiousfreedom_209-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-religiousfreedom-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> Among Emirati Muslim citizens, 97% are <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni</a>, while 3% are <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam_in_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="Shia Islam in the United Arab Emirates">Shi'a</a>, mostly concentrated in the emirates of Sharjah and <a href="/wiki/Dubai" title="Dubai">Dubai</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-religiousfreedom_209-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-religiousfreedom-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> Omani immigrants are mostly <a href="/wiki/Ibadi" title="Ibadi">Ibadi</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Sufi" class="mw-redirect" title="Sufi">Sufi</a> influences exist too.<sup id="cite_ref-371" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-371">&#91;371&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Arab_Emirates&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a> is the national language of the United Arab Emirates. The <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Arabic" title="Gulf Arabic">Gulf dialect</a> of Arabic is spoken natively by the Emirati people.<sup id="cite_ref-372" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-372">&#91;372&#93;</a></sup> Since the area was occupied by the British until 1971,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (January 2018)">dubious</span></a>&#32;<span class="metadata"> &#8211; <a href="/wiki/Talk:United_Arab_Emirates#Dubious" title="Talk:United Arab Emirates">discuss</a></span></i>&#93;</sup> English is the primary <i><a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a></i> in the UAE. As such, a knowledge of the language is a requirement when applying for most local jobs.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Arab_Emirates&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_the_United_Arab_Emirates" title="Health in the United Arab Emirates">Health in the United Arab Emirates</a></div>
<p>The life expectancy at birth in the UAE is at 76.96 years.<sup id="cite_ref-373" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-373">&#91;373&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cardiovascular_disease" title="Cardiovascular disease">Cardiovascular disease</a> is the principal cause of death in the UAE, constituting 28% of total deaths; other major causes are <a href="/wiki/Accident" title="Accident">accidents</a> and <a href="/wiki/Injury" title="Injury">injuries</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cancer" title="Cancer">malignancies</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Congenital_disorder" class="mw-redirect" title="Congenital disorder">congenital anomalies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cp_374-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cp-374">&#91;374&#93;</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Body_Mass_Index_(BMI)#WHO_Data_on_Prevalence_of_Obesity_(BMI_above_30)_(2014)" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries by Body Mass Index (BMI)">World Health Organisation data from 2014</a>, 37.2% of adults in the UAE are clinically <a href="/wiki/Obesity" title="Obesity">obese</a>, with a <a href="/wiki/Body_mass_index" title="Body mass index">Body mass index</a> (BMI) score of 30 or more.<sup id="cite_ref-375" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-375">&#91;375&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2008, the Ministry of Health unveiled a five-year health strategy for the public health sector in the northern emirates, which fall under its purview and which, unlike Abu Dhabi and Dubai, do not have separate healthcare authorities. The strategy focuses on unifying
healthcare policy and improving access to healthcare services at reasonable cost, at the same time reducing dependence on overseas treatment. The ministry plans to add three hospitals to the current 14, and 29 primary healthcare centres to the current 86. Nine were scheduled to open in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-376" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-376">&#91;376&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The introduction of mandatory <a href="/wiki/Health_insurance" title="Health insurance">health insurance</a> in Abu Dhabi for <a href="/wiki/Expatriate" title="Expatriate">expatriates</a> and their dependants was a major driver in reform of healthcare policy. Abu Dhabi nationals were brought under the scheme from 1 June 2008 and Dubai followed for its government employees. Eventually, under federal law, every Emirati and expatriate in the country will be covered by compulsory health insurance under a unified mandatory scheme.<sup id="cite_ref-377" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-377">&#91;377&#93;</a></sup>
The country has benefited from medical tourists from all over the <a href="/wiki/Cooperation_Council_for_the_Arab_States_of_the_Gulf" class="mw-redirect" title="Cooperation Council for the Arab States of the Gulf">Cooperation Council for the Arab States of the Gulf</a>. The UAE attracts medical tourists seeking plastic surgery and advanced procedures, cardiac and spinal surgery, and dental treatment, as health services have higher standards than other Arab countries in the Persian Gulf.<sup id="cite_ref-thenational.ae_378-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thenational.ae-378">&#91;378&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<li id="cite_note-22"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-22">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Al Qasimi, Muhammad (1986). <i>The Myth of Piracy in the Arabian Gulf</i>. UK: Croom Helm. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0709921063" title="Special:BookSources/0709921063"><bdi>0709921063</bdi></a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Myth+of+Piracy+in+the+Arabian+Gulf&amp;rft.place=UK&amp;rft.pub=Croom+Helm&amp;rft.date=1986&amp;rft.isbn=0709921063&amp;rft.aulast=Al+Qasimi&amp;rft.aufirst=Muhammad&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AUnited+Arab+Emirates" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/> Note: "The term <i>Pirate Coast</i> was first used by the British around the 17th century and acquired its name from the raiding activities that <a href="/wiki/Al_Qawasim" class="mw-redirect" title="Al Qawasim">Al Qawasim</a> pursued against the British. The charge of piracy has been disputed by historians and archivists in the UAE in particular. The counter-argument is that the Al Qasimi were the subject of British aggression in an attempt to stamp its authority on trade routes thought of as important to Iraq and India"</span>

<li id="cite_note-146"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-146">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.thenational.ae/news/uae-news/courts/dh500-000-expat-verbal-abuse-case-to-be-retried">"Dh500,000 expat verbal abuse case to be retried"</a>. <i>The National</i>. 8 December 2010. <q>In the UAE, only verbal abuse pertaining to the sexual honour of a person would be tried under Sharia. For guilt to be proven, the attack must have been made in public and one reliable witness must testify. <li id="cite_note-230"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-230">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://2009-2017.state.gov/j/drl/rls/hrrpt/2000/nea/824.htm">"United Arab Emirates – Country Reports on Human Rights Practices"</a>. <q>In February an Indonesian woman convicted of adultery by the Shari'a court in the Emirate of Fujairah, was sentenced to death by stoning after she purportedly insisted on such punishment.  The sentence was commuted on appeal to 1 year in prison, followed by deportation. In June 1998, the Shari'a court in Fujairah sentenced three Omani nationals convicted of robbery to have their right hands amputated. The Fujairah prosecutor's office instead commuted the sentence to a term of imprisonment.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=United+Arab+Emirates+%E2%80%93+Country+Reports+on+Human+Rights+Practices&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2F2009-2017.state.gov%2Fj%2Fdrl%2Frls%2Fhrrpt%2F2000%2Fnea%2F824.htm&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AUnited+Arab+Emirates" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>
